So awesome!  I did not know that consomme was so I just bought beef broth. Before I made the recipe I looked it up and realized it is a strong broth so I just added 3 beef bullion cubes to the broth before adding the roast beef. It was so great. Everyone in my family gobbled it up. My husband preferred cheddar and and mustard so it was easy to change it up before putting in the oven.

It does't get much easier than this! Plus, it tastes really good! All I added to the "au jus" was a 1 tsp. of minced garlic, and a 1/2 tsp. of rosemary. I also sauteed a large onion sliced into 1/2 inch rings. I used swiss cheese instead of provolone (personal preference). These were some "Easiest" French Dip sanwiches ever!

text:
I made this for my son and I tonight.  He said this is better than Arby's!  I did make a few changes.  I added onion powder, garlic powder, and pepper to the beef broth like others did.  I sauteed green bell pepper, onion and mushroom to add to sandwich under the provolone.  Gotta get them veggies in!  I am still trying to find the bread that will hold up to the juice as the hoagie turns too mushy, maybe toasting it as others have done will make the difference.  I'll try that next time.  I have found that the sandwich turns out best with good quality meat from the deli.  This is a keeper for my family as we can customize to individual tastes, quick to prepare and yummy.

text:
Very easy. I've used consomme forever due to it's weight & flavor.  However, absolutely NOT a fan of deli roast beef b/c it does not even resemb le real roast beef in flavor.  I take a 4 lb.boneless beef roast from the freezer, place it in a 500 degree oven for 30-45 mins.  Turn oven down to 250 and roast UNcoveredfor 6 hrs.  The finished product is fantastic & the drippings must  be moistened, stirred up & added to the consomme.  This is the only way to eat roast beef in our family.

text:
Toasting the hougie does make a difference.  I toast the bread with garlic butter until it is crispy.  Occasionally; I'll add provolone or Swiss cheese during the toasting.  This seals the bread and allows the au jus to slowly mix into the bread.  I have also used the au jus as a dipping sauce only, that way the bread soaks up the au jus at the time you eat it.  Either way, this is a great sandwich and a regular at my home.

region:
None
country:
None
text:
Saute a few onions and green peppers in butter. (Add a few slices of fresh jalapeno if you are courageous.) Set that aside and warm the beef in the same pan with a little Au Jus. Pile that warm beef into a hollowed out hoagie bun that has been smeared with horseradish sauce. Pile those yummy peppers and onion on top, followed by the cheese - I use Swiss - then pop it in the oven ntil the cheese melts. As far as the Au Jus, amp that dry mix up by substituting brandy or wine for some of the water and throw in a bit of fresh ground pepper.
Yowser, from dud to stud!

text:
I have been making these sandwiches for years. Here is how I make mine. I use Au Jus and sometimes swiss cheese. I put the meat in the au jus and to warm it. Meanwhile, I butter the hoagie rolls and put them under the broiler just to brown. Then, I put the meat and cheese on one side of bun and put back under the broiler until the cheese is melted and starts to brown. Then it is a matter of preference. Serve as is are put mayo and/or mustard on the top bun. sever with a dipping bowl of Au Jus. So good.

text:
I have been making my own version of this for years and it's awsome.  I prefer it open faced.  I make this any time I have made a roast and have left overs.  I use crisp Italian buns, slice off the top as little as I can to leave the widest surface of the bun.  I sautee  a bunch of onions and use a packaged au jus dip.  I slice/dice up the leftovers and  warm them up using a bit of the au jus.  Then just load up the bun, layer with lots of onions, top with usually swiss cheese and broil until cheese has melted and slightly grilled.  Ready to serve.  Sometimes I use the shaved off top portion to cover or just use it to dip in the jus.  Either way, not only is it so simple, the presentation is equally as great.  Even when I haven't made a roast in a while, I'll grab some roast beef from the deli just to get "our fix".  When you want it, you want it!

text:
This is a simple recipe. I am from NYC.  In NYC they only dip the roast beef in the hot beef juice.  Then they dip the top part of the roll in the juice. John's Deli in Bensonhurst Brooklyn is famous for this. In Upstate they use a Kaiser roll and brush the top with water and sprinkle course salt and caraway seeds on top and bake for a few minutes.  They do the exact same dipping.  This is a Beef on Wick.  To make it great you need to put fresh horseradish on the sandwich and skip the cheese.  I mean really fresh.  To make fresh horseradish, find the root in a fruit market, peel it with a knife, cut it into small pieces and then grind it up in a blender adding white vinegar.  Keep the room well ventilated and have a glass container ready to put it into.  Yummy!

mmmm...this was DELICIOUS!  I actually modified the recipe.  I bought 1/2 pound thinly sliced roast beef, and 1/2 pound angus roast beef thinly sliced from the deli.  For my juice I boiled 2 cups of water and added a little more than 2 tsp of boullion granuals.  I mixed that up and put it all together in a pot on low to simmer.  I cut up 4 bakery buns, topped with roast beef, and thinly shredded mozzarella. Then I stuck it under the broiler until the cheese was melted and served with some of the juice in a cup for dipping.  It was DELICIOUS!!

Thanks for the recipe idea!

I bought premium Boar's Head roast beef and good quality provolone.  Added some minced garlic to the au jus sauce, just heated up the roast beef in the broth - no slow cooking required!  I sauteed shallot, mushrooms and sliced red pepper.  Each sandwich had the beef/veggie combo topped with provolone and back in the oven to melt the cheese.  Divine! For the vegetarian diet stepdaughter I loaded up a roll with the veggies and melted the cheese like the others.  This is in the regular rotation, for sure.

text:
these were great! very easy like the title says! i did toast my bread in the oven first for about 3 min to cut down any sogginess, which worked well. i also used one slice of cheese on bottom as well as top. i used an au jus packet that came free with the purchase of my roast beef (deli promotion) and added extra water and beef granules and added garlic powder and black pepper to the broth. i sauteed red peppers and onions in separate pans and made each sandwich to order. 1# of roast beef made 6 sandwiches.  also cup up some jalapenos and set on the table for whoever wanted an extra kick! there were NO leftovers!

This was a great quick weeknight meal.  My husband loved it as much as when I would cook a roast in the crock pot all day for au jus sandwiches.  I wish I new about this shortcut earlier!  I sauteed some onions for our sandwiches and toasted the bread before putting the sandwiches together.  That will help your bread from getting too soggy too quickly.

Wow. This was soo easy - and soo delicious.  My husband even said that it was better than Phillipe's (LA's "Birthplace of the French Dip").  I added some garlic powder, Worcestershire sauce, and butter to taste.  I used Demi Baguettes and toasted them a bit in the oven before adding the meat and cheese.  I also poured the au jus onto the bread, soaking it a bit, before putting it back into the oven to melt the cheese.  Turned out DELICIOUS!

text:
It's not often leftovers make a meal comparably enjoyable to one freshly made. I will make sure I always buy a roast beef a bit bigger just for this reason. A Sunday roast dinner can be stretched to another day as thinly sliced leftover beef is piled high atop soft crispy buns. I am a beef lover but do not care for it from the deli. Using leftover meat is far less expensive and cooked the way you like it. I don't use consomme very often and had forgotton its nice smooth flavour. Rather than water I added 1 cup of low-sodium beef oxo/water. I chose to carmelized some onions and had to use motzerella cheese. This was served on the freshest buns I could find. Dinner was on the table in under 20 minutes. Five stars for quick, inexpensive and exceptional good eats!

text:
Ahhhh-mazing!! I was skeptical about using deli roast beef but it turned out so good!  I did make some changes though. I used the McCormick au jus packet. It has so much flavor that you don't need to add a thing. Just follow the prep instructions on the packet.  For the roast beef, I bought the Dietz & Watson brand. It is super expensive at $13 / lb but it made all the difference. For the bread, I used a fresh baked french loaf from my grocery store's bakery.

The french loaf was the perfect size to cut into 4 sandwiches. Once I split the bread open, I spread a little bit of butter on the inside before adding the beef.

As for the roast beef, I prefer mine on the rarer side, so I only put mine into the hot au jus just long enough to saturate without cooking it further.

It turned out so amazing and my family scarfed it down! It seriously could have passed for a meal at an upscale restaurant! I was super impressed. :)  The only thing I would do differently next time is probably broil the sandwiches for the last minute. I didn't feel they were quite hot enough after only 5 minutes in a 350 degree oven. Plus, I like my cheese to be super melted with a little bit of browning.

Display Name:

photo:
https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/5614247.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I had seven to feed so I bought 2 pounds of  deli meat (thinly sliced). 1 or 2 cloves chopped garlic,  pan-cooked in butter for a minute in a large pot, then added 32 oz beef broth, 1 cup water, and 1 rounded Tbsp. of bullion paste. Saute onion s a red pepper strips, lightly salted, on the side, as an optional topping to add. I broke meat into about four sections to warm together in broth and then set the meat in a strainer over the broth to minimize the drippiness before adding to the oven-toasted buns. It was a BIG hit and my husband has already requested an encore!

I place the beef on a cutting board and make one inch cuts across it.  Cut one bell pepper in slices, slice one medium or large onion and cut across rings a few times.  Spray a skillet and soften pepper and onions.  Add beef and stir a few minutes.  Place meat on hoagie rolls, cover with provolone  and broil open face. Serve with packaged au jus made up with a tbsp of flour.

text:
We have made these 3 times in the past 2 weeks.  Super simple and easy to customize.  I know some people get frustrated when a reviewer makes changes, but that's  part of cooking.  I do add a couple cloves of finely chopped garlic and 1/4 tsp of red pepper flake to the au jus and let it simmer for an hour.  Do saute red onion and sliced mushrooms.  Do mix some sweet-hot mustard with a bit of mayo and butter the rolls with it.   The recipe also allows for making 90% of it ahead of time, then just pop it in the oven when ready.  Love it  !!

region:

country:
None
text:
I really enjoyed this recipe.  It was so easy, quick, and inexpensive. A few things to note (none of these changes were used in rating this recipe)-  I couldn't find beef consomm√© at the store, so I bought beef broth with the intention of adding some beef bouillon to it once home, only to find out I was out of bouillon.  Despite adding onion powder, garlic powder, and some black pepper, the broth was still a little too bland for me.  So I would encourage making sure you start off with the consomm√© (or at least add a little bouillon) if you like a stronger broth flavor.  Like other reviewers suggested, I toasted my bread before hand and didn't have any issues with the rolls getting soggy.  I also used swiss instead of provolone (personal preference).  

The only thing that kept this recipe from being 5 stars was the fact that heating the meat in the broth both dried out and toughened it.  Dipping the sandwich made it moist once more but I could still notice a texture difference in the meat.  (Perhaps I left it in the broth too long or at too high a temp?)  

I will definitely make this again but with the stronger broth and possibly some grilled onions. Thanks for the recipe!
